                 LOS RIOS COMMUNITY COLLEGE DISTRICT
PRESENTED TO BOARD OF TRUSTEES                                                 DATE: February 18, 2026

   SUBJECT:                   Board Policy Amendments: P-8431       ATTACHMENT: Yes
                              Naming of Facilities and Areas
                                                                    ENCLOSURE: None
                                                                    STRATEGIC PLAN GOAL(S): 5
   AGENDA ITEM:               First Reading Item B                  TYPE OF BOARD CONSIDERATION:

                                                                    CONSENT/ROUTINE
   RECOMMENDED BY:            Paula Allison, Chief Advancement                                      X
                                                                    FIRST READING
                              Officer
   APPROVED FOR                                                     ACTION
   CONSIDERATION:
                              Brian King, Chancellor                INFORMATION

BACKGROUND:
Changes to Policy 8431 are being proposed with the intention of increasing private giving to the
District and reserving naming opportunities primarily to donors making financial contributions. The
revised policy also creates a distinction between “Major Facilities” and “Minor Properties.” Board
approval would be required for the naming of Major Facilities, while the Chancellor (with the ability to
delegate to the College President) would have the authority to approve naming of Minor Properties.
For both Major Facilities and Minor Properties, the policy provides for consultation with the
appropriate College constituencies before naming or recommending a name to the Board. The
updated policy also adds terms for corporate namings. Changes to the policy are largely modeled off
CSU and UC’s naming policies and were developed in consultation with external counsel with
statewide expertise in this area.

STATUS:
The proposed changes to Policy 8431, if adopted, would align the District’s Naming Policy with related
UC and CSU policies and help increase private giving to the District.

RECOMMENDATION:
This policy is presented for first reading.




                                                                                                   126
                                                                                                          HOME
 BUILDING CONSTRUCTION PROGRAM                           Naming of Facilities and Areas       P-8431

 Memorials                                                                                     1 of 6


1.0 Purpose
The Los Rios Community College District has a long-standing practice of naming District
property after persons or entities who have made important contributions to the District, whether
financial or otherwise. This Policy governs those practices, with a focus on and intention of
increasing private giving to the District, reserving naming opportunities primarily to donors
making financial contributions to the District needed to support its Colleges and students.
Namings without private support are permissible but are reserved for the most exceptional
circumstances.

1.02.0 Authority & Responsibility for Making Recommendations
       2.1     The following bodies and individuals have authority to approve proposed naming
               opportunities, as outlined below:

               2.1.1   The Los Rios Community College District’s Board of Trustees shall has
                       the authority to approve the naming of the facilities and propertiesareas of
                       the Los Rios Community College District and its Colleges and to delegate
                       the review and approval of such namings, as it has done so in this Policy
                       or otherwise elects to do so in the future. The Board of Trustees further
                       reserves the right to waive the requirements of this Policy.

               2.1.2   The Board of Trustees reserves to itself the authority to approve
                       recommended namings for buildings and major portions of buildings;
                       stadiums, arenas, athletic fields, and other highly visible facilities and
                       properties (each a “Major Facility”).

               2.1.3   The Board of Trustees delegates to the Chancellor the authority to name
                       minor properties, including plazas, courtyards, classrooms, offices,
                       conference rooms, lounges, laboratories, studios, and rooms within
                       buildings (each a “Minor Property”). The Chancellor may sub-delegate the
                       authority to name a Minor Property to a College President, at the
                       Chancellor’s discretion.

               2.1.4   Non-public facing spaces with limited public exposure or small or
                       temporary items, such as benches, small landscape features, fountains,
                       trees, gardens, bricks, donor walls, and equipment or collections are
                       excluded from this Policy and any namings with respect to such spaces or
                       items may be approved by the College Presidents or their designees.

       2.2     The Los Rios Colleges Foundation (Foundation) does not have the authority to
               approve naming proposals. Instead, the Foundation is expected to and shall make
               naming recommendations in connection with its philanthropic activities, to the
               Board of Trustees, Chancellor, or College Presidents, depending on who has
               authority to approve the type of naming at issue, consistent with the requirements
               of this Policy.

                                                                                                    127
                                                                                                    HOME
BUILDING CONSTRUCTION PROGRAM                        Naming of Facilities and Areas      P-8431

Memorials                                                                                 2 of 6

     2.3    The College Presidents and the Chancellor also have the authority to make
            proposed naming recommendations with respect to Major Facilities to the Board
            of Trustees.

     1.1    The Board of Trustees may seek the advice of the Los Rios Colleges Foundation
            in making a decision to name a particular building or area.

     1.2    The Chancellor and the Los Rios Colleges Foundation may recommend approval
            of exceptions to this District Policy.

2.03.0 Principles, Guidelines, and Requirements that Apply to All
   Namings
     3.1    Buildings and areas may be named in honor of friends, benefactors, and persons
            who have made significant contributions to the College, the District, or to
            education in California or the nation.

     3.1    The naming of a building or place is a matter of serious commitment, with long-
            term implications for the District. Accordingly, no naming may be approved on a
            commitment. The choice to give a personal name to a building implies permanent
            basis. Instead, for all namings, the District reserves the right to remove a naming
            if the Board of Trustees or its designee determines, in its sole discretion, that the
            naming could adversely impact the reputation, image, mission, or integrity of the
            District or the Colleges or is no longer in the best interests of the District or the
            Colleges. The Board of Trustees further reserves the right to remove a naming,
            whether on a Major Facility or Minor Property, in the event of significant
            renovation, repurposing, or relocation of the facility or area where the naming is
            located. Renaming may also occur when a facility or area has reached the end of
            its useful life. Any approval of a naming pursuant to this Policy is subject to these
            reserved rights. The Foundation and District and College administration shall take
            care to memorialize these rights as is appropriate under the given circumstances,
            such as in a donor agreement, but the failure to do so shall not render or void the
            reservation of rights in this Policy and any approval of a naming shall nonetheless
            be subject to these reservations of rightspermanence of that designation—both in
            terms of the designation itself and to the maintenance and refurbishment of the
            building. The naming opportunity thus has both moral and financial implications.
            The District reserves the right to remove the name of a building in the appropriate
            circumstances.

     3.2    Subunits of a new or existing building may be named separately to recognize an
            outstanding individual or a donor wishing to contribute the cost of a portion of a
            building, a room in a building, a major equipment item, a major art feature or
            water feature, and the like.


     3.2    Buildings and areas may be named for persons who: have rendered significant,
            permanent service to education in California or the nation; who have
            distinguished themselves in the work of a College, campus, discipline, or
                                                                                            128
                                                                                                    HOME
BUILDING CONSTRUCTION PROGRAM                        Naming of Facilities and Areas      P-8431

Memorials                                                                                 3 of 6

            department within the District; who are indigenous to the area and hold a unique
            place in history; or have made a substantial gift to the College or the District
            through its official fundraising arm, the Los Rios Colleges Foundation.

     3.3    Buildings and areas may not be named for current District employees. When an
            area or building is proposed to be named for individuals associated with the
            District or California education, a period of not less than three years should elapse
            between the end of the individual’s service to the District or California education
            and consideration by the Board of Trustees.

     3.3    No facility or property will be named after seated, elected, or appointed officials
            currently in office.

     3.4    In all instances where the word “person,” “individual,” or “donor,” is used in this
            District Policy, the same shall be deemed to include corporations, foundations, or
            other appropriate legal entities.

     3.5    When the Board of Trustees, Chancellor, or a President is considering a naming
            proposal, they shall consider, among other things: whether the proposed naming
            would lend prestige to the District, College, staff, students, and community; the
            credentials, character, and reputation of the person; and the person’s contribution,
            including any monetary donations to support the District or its Colleges; and any
            potential costs associated with the naming.

     3.6    The Chancellor or College Presidents shall consult with the appropriate College
            constituencies (including, but not limited to, the Academic Senate, the Classified
            Senate, the Student Body Associations, etc.) before bringing a recommendation to
            the Board of Trustees to name a Major Facility. The Chancellor or the College
            Presidents shall also consult with the Executive Vice Chancellor Finance and the
            Chief Advancement Officer prior to presenting recommendations to the Board of
            Trustees with respect to naming a Major Facility.

     3.7    The Chancellor or College Presidents shall consult with the Executive Vice
            Chancellor Finance, the Chief Advancement Officer and the appropriate College
            constituencies (including, but not limited to, the Academic Senate, the Classified
            Senate, the Student Body Associations, etc.) prior to naming a Minor Property.

     3.8    Proposals for namings shall be submitted in writing and should identify and
            discuss the considerations outlined in this Policy and any other relevant
            considerations, as well as how the District will memorialize its reservation of
            rights listed above in the Policy.


3.0 Guidelines
     3.1    Names of facilities or areas should lend prestige to the District/College, and to
            staff, students, and community. The credentials, character, and reputation of each
            individual for whom the naming of a building is being considered shall be

                                                                                              129
                                                                                                     HOME
BUILDING CONSTRUCTION PROGRAM                         Naming of Facilities and Areas       P-8431

Memorials                                                                                  4 of 6

            carefully scrutinized and evaluated. Nominations submitted to the Board of
            Trustees for consideration shall be accompanied by appropriate supporting
            documentation.

     3.2    The College Presidents shall consult with the appropriate College constituencies
            (including, but not limited to, the Academic Senate, the Classified Senate, the
            Student Body Associations, etc.) before bringing a recommendation to the
            Chancellor to name a building or an area under this District Policy. The Presidents
            shall also consult with the Vice Chancellor, Finance and Administration, and the
            Associate Vice Chancellor, Resource Development prior to presenting
            recommendations to the Chancellor. The Chancellor shall present
            recommendations for naming to the Board.

     3.3    A financial gift shall not automatically result in the naming of a building for an
            individual. The other criteria of this District Policy must also be met.

     3.4    In addition to the permanent nature of a facility named to honor an individual,
            shorter-term issues—such as name plaques, stationery, catalog listings, maps,
            ceremonial action, and publicity—shall be considered.

     3.5    A suitable plaque should be located in the lobby or other significant location,
            giving the full name and brief biography of the person honored.

4.0 Namings Provided to Thank a Donor
     4.1    The vast majority of namings should be made solely in connection with
            donations, because naming opportunities provide a significant way of
            incentivizing philanthropic support for the District and its Colleges and are a
            means of thanking donors.

     4.2    When reviewing a naming proposal in connection with a donation, the following
            additional factors may be considered, in addition to the general considerations
            listed above:

            4.2.1   The significance of the proposed donation in contributing to the success or
                    realization of a capital campaign, construction project, or other fundraising
                    related project;

            4.2.2   The urgency of the fundraising related project’s need or the need for
                    funding support;

            4.2.3   The individual’s relationship to the District;

            4.2.4   Whether the individual or entity has made other substantial gifts to the
                    College or the District through the Foundation or otherwise.

     4.3    When an individual donor gift is involved, the naming shall be for the useful life
            of the facility or for a defined period of years. The useful life is generally defined
            as until the facility or property is destroyed or substantially renovated.
                                                                                               130
                                                                                                     HOME
BUILDING CONSTRUCTION PROGRAM                        Naming of Facilities and Areas      P-8431

Memorials                                                                                  5 of 6

     4.4    Namings after corporations, businesses, or other commercial entities (whether
            operated for profit or not) may only be approved in connection with a significant
            donation to support the District or its Colleges. Any such naming after a
            corporation, business or other commercial entity must be limited to a defined
            number of years.

     4.5    When a corporate or commercial entity is involved, the size, design, and wording
            of plaques and other signs that are in connection with the donation should be
            modest in size and exclude corporate logos to avoid the appearance of advertising.

     4.6    A financial gift shall not automatically result in a naming, whether a Major
            Facility or Minor Property, for an individual.

5.0 Namings to Honor a Member of the Community
     5.1    In rare instances, when there is a proposal to provide a naming to a person to
            honor them, unconnected to a donation from that person, the proposal should
            address and demonstrate how that person has demonstrated distinction in one or
            more of the following ways:

            5.1.1   Academic Service: The individual has shown outstanding scholarly
                    achievement and earned a strong national or international scholarly
                    reputation while serving the institution in an academic role.

            5.1.2   Exceptional Contribution or Distinction: The individual has made
                    extraordinary contributions to the District or achieved a level of distinction
                    that justifies formal recognition.

     5.2    Honorary names of Major Facilities shall be proposed to the Board upon the
            advice and recommendation of the Chancellor. Honorary names of Minor
            Properties must be approved directly by the Chancellor and College President,
            consistent with any delegation of authority under this Policy.

     5.3    Naming proposals after current District employees are not permitted. When an
            area or building is proposed to be named for former employees with the District, a
            period of not less than three years should elapse between the end of the
            individual’s service to the District and the naming proposal.


4.06.0 Guidelines Regarding Uniformity in Signage and StyleUse of
   Names
     6.1    A uniform system of marking of buildings and outdoor areas should be adopted
            by location.

     6.2    Plaques and signage should be tasteful, discrete, and consistent with other campus
            signage as determined by the Associate Vice Chancellor of Facilities
            Management.
                                                                                             131
                                                                                                   HOME
BUILDING CONSTRUCTION PROGRAM                        Naming of Facilities and Areas      P-8431

Memorials                                                                                 6 of 6

     6.3    When honoring an individual and using a plaque, the plaque should be located in
            the lobby or other significant location, giving the full name and brief biography of
            the person honored.

     6.36.4 To minimize exterior lettering, listings in directories, mailing addresses, and the
            like, as well as to ensure that the use of the new name becomes commonplace
            within the lexicon of the College and District, the naming of a building to honor
            an individual should use the surname only, as in “Raef Hall” and “Rodda Hall.”

5.0 Portions of Buildings
     5.1    Subunits of a new or existing building may be named separately to recognize an
            outstanding individual or a donor wishing to contribute the cost of a portion of a
            building, a room in a building, a major equipment item, a major art feature or
            water feature, and the like.

     5.2    In cases where the feature is named after an individual pursuant to this District
            Policy, the committee or group making such a recommendation shall identify, or
            provide the source for the full cost of changing the name, such cost being
            determined by the Associate Vice Chancellor of Facilities Management.

     5.3    Non-public facing spaces with limited exposure are excluded from the naming
            requirement. This includes small landscape features, fountains, trees, gardens,
            benches, temporary facilities items, equipment or collections, campus donor walls
            or similar items.

                                      (Formerly P-4623)

                LOS RIOS COMMUNITY COLLEGE DISTRICT
PRESENTED TO BOARD OF TRUSTEES                                                    DATE: February 18, 2026

   SUBJECT:                   Resolution No. 2026:04: Declaring       ATTACHMENT: Yes
                              Intention to a Form School Facilities
                              Improvement District                    ENCLOSURE: None
                                                                      STRATEGIC PLAN GOAL(S): 1, 5
   AGENDA ITEM:              First Reading Item C                     TYPE OF BOARD CONSIDERATION:


                              Mario Rodriguez, Executive              CONSENT/ROUTINE
   RECOMMENDED BY:            Vice Chancellor, Finance and
                                                                      FIRST READING                   X
                              Administration
   APPROVED FOR                                                       ACTION
   CONSIDERATION:
                              Brian King, Chancellor                  INFORMATION

BACKGROUND:
State law authorizes community college districts to form a sub-territory within their boundaries, each
designated as a school facilities improvement district (SFID), and to thereafter call a general obligation
bond election within that sub-territory. If the election is successful, voter-approved general obligation
bonds may be issued, with the proceeds applied to improve facilities within the SFID.

STATUS:
District staff has identified facilities needs within the portions of the District located in Sacramento and
Yolo counties. Accordingly, staff recommends establishing a SFID whose boundaries encompass those
areas. A proposed boundary map is included in this board agenda item. If a SFID is formed following the
public hearing at the March meeting, the District Board has the option by subsequent Board action adopt
a resolution placing a general obligation bond measure before voters of the SFID in accordance with the
procedures of Proposition 39, which permits a 55% bond measure to be placed before voters in
November 2026.

Steps of formation of a SFID consist of (1) Board action adopting a Resolution of Intention to Form a SFID
which contains the required legal recitals, (2) conduct a Public Hearing on Formation following public
notice, and (3) Board action adopting a Resolution of Formation. The public hearing and formation are
currently expected at the March 11, 2026, Board meeting.

RECOMMENDATION:
This resolution is presented for first reading.




                                                                                                     138
                                                                                                           HOME




                LOS RIOS COMMUNITY COLLEGE DISTRICT
                         American River ▪ Cosumnes River ▪ Folsom Lake ▪ Sacramento City Colleges



                                 RESOLUTION
                                              № 2026-04

        Declaring Intention to a Form School Facilities Improvement District


        WHEREAS, the California Education Code commencing at Section 15300 and following
(the “SFID Law”) provides a method for the formation of school facilities improvement districts
consisting of a portion of the territory within a school district or a community college district formed
for the purpose of conducting a bond election within said school facilities improvement district; and

        WHEREAS, upon the formation of a school facilities improvement district and following the
conduct of a successful general obligation bond election within said territory, general obligation
bonds may be issued, the proceeds of which will be applied to finance voter-approved facilities
projects within said school facilities improvement district; and

       WHEREAS, the Los Rios Community College District (the “District”), with territory located
across five counties, including primarily in the County of Sacramento, but including territory
located in the counties of El Dorado, Yolo, Solano and Placer, has undertaken facilities needs
assessments and studies which have identified important facilities improvement needs which need
to be addressed, including specifically with respect to its facilities located in the counties of
Sacramento and Yolo; and

       WHEREAS, a local funding source such as the proceeds of a general obligation bond
measure is necessary to address said educational facilities needs, with the desired outcome of
taxpayer funds staying local, with no voter-approved funds going to state or federal entities; and

       WHEREAS, with California’s high unemployment rates the District and its American River,
Cosumnes River, Folsom Lake and Sacramento City colleges, seeks to upgrade facilities and
programs for technology, software development and engineering, nursing and other medical
professionals, firefighters, law enforcement, and other first responders; and

       WHEREAS, the District’s colleges also must address core upgrades such as removing
asbestos and lead pipe, providing safe, clean drinking water and repairing leaky roofs; and

         WHEREAS, to that end, in the judgment of the Board of Trustees (the “Board”) of the
District, it is advisable and necessary at this time to commence the process of forming a sub-area
within the District consisting of the territory of the District located in the counties of Sacramento
and Yolo, to be known as a school facilities improvement district, all pursuant to the proceedings
available in the SFID Law, and following said formation, to call and conduct a general obligation
bond election therein all for the purpose of obtaining a local financing source for facilities
improvements within the territory located in the counties of Sacramento and Yolo counties and
which will benefit the properties in said areas; and

       WHEREAS, on September 10, 2004, the Yolo County Board of Supervisors adopted
Resolution No. 04-148 making the SFID Law applicable in Yolo County;

      WHEREAS, on December 16, 2025, the Sacramento County Board of Supervisors
adopted Resolution No. 2025-0804 making the SFID Law applicable in Sacramento County;139
                                                                                                              HOME



          WHEREAS, as part of the legal process required to form a school facilities improvement
district, the SFID Law requires the Board to adopt a resolution declaring certain matters, including
(i) its intent to form a school facilities improvement district, (ii) the purpose for which the district is
to be formed, (iii) the estimated cost of the project(s) for which the improvement district is being
formed and (iv) establishing the time and place for a public hearing by the Board on the proposed
school facilities improvement district: Now, therefore,

        BE IT RESOLVED as follows:

        Section 1. Recitals. The foregoing recitals are true and correct.

       Section 2. Intent to Form a School Facilities Improvement District. The Board hereby
declares it is necessary and in the best interests of the District for form a school facilities
improvement district in the District territory located in the Sacramento County and Yolo County.
The Board declares its intent to form a school facilities improvement district to be identified as
“School Facilities Improvement District No. 1 of the Los Rios Community College District” (the
“Improvement District”) within the boundaries of the District.

         Section 3. Purposes of Formation of the Improvement District. The Board is forming
the Improvement District for the purpose of financing school facilities improvement projects within
the boundaries of the Improvement District, including the construction, reconstruction,
rehabilitation, and replacement of school facilities, the furnishing and equipping of school facilities,
and/or the acquisition or lease of real property for school facilities, which are the types of projects
that can be presented more particularly to voters in a general obligation bond measure or
measures presented to voters of the Improvement District in accordance with the provisions of
law implemented with Proposition 39, and all of which will benefit the land within the Improvement
District (collectively referred to herein as the “Improvement Projects”). The Board may more
particularly define the Improvement Projects to be addressed with the proceeds of a bond
measure in the text of a general obligation bond measure or measures, called in accordance with
the SFID Law.

        Section 4. Estimated Cost of the Improvement Projects. The District has conducted a
recent facilities assessment that has identified approximately $3.1 billion in facilities needs and
Improvement Projects in the Improvement District. Notwithstanding this foregoing cost estimate,
general obligation bonds, if approved, will only be issued in a principal amount which does not
exceed the amount presented to and approved by voters of the Improvement District, which may
occur at one or more bond elections to be held and conducted in the future in accordance with all
legal requirements.

         Section 5. Levy of Taxes Only Within Improvement District. If the issuance of general
obligation bonds is approved in accordance with California law by the voters of the Improvement
District, all taxes levied for the purpose of paying principal of and interest on any such general
obligation bonds shall be levied exclusively upon the lands in the Improvement District, and not
on any other land in the District that is not within the boundaries of the Improvement District.

        Section 6. Boundary Map. In accordance with Education Code Section 15320(e), a map
showing the exterior boundaries of the proposed Improvement District meeting the requirements
of Education Code Section 15301 is on file with the Board and is hereby approved and available
for public inspection at the Office of the Chancellor during regular business hours. Education Code
Section 15301(b) does not apply because the District has not formed a community facilities district
as provided therein.

       Section 7. Public Hearing. The Board will conduct a public hearing on the proposed
formation of the Improvement District at which any interested persons, including all persons
owning land in the District or in the Improvement District, may appear and be heard. The date
and time of the public hearing is as follows:                                           140
                                                                                                            HOME



                           Date:        Wednesday, March 11, 2026
                           Time:        5:30 PM (Approximately)
                           Location:    District Board Room at 1919 Spanos Court, Sacramento, CA

        Section 8. Notice of Public Hearing: Publication. Pursuant to the Law, the District
shall cause this Resolution to be published in a newspaper of general circulation in each affected
county, being Sacramento County and Yolo County, in advance of the public hearing. Said
publication shall occur once a week for two successive weeks, in accordance with Government
Code Section 6066, beginning no later than 14 days prior to the date set for the public hearing.

         Section 9. Additional Findings. The District has not previously created community
facilities districts pursuant to Government Code Section 53311 and following which have
boundaries that overlap with the proposed Improvement District and as such, Education Code
15301 (a) and (b) do not apply. The Board determines that it is necessary and in the best interest
of the District to form a school facilities improvement district pursuant to the SFID law to finance
facilities and purposes authorized by Education Code Section 15100. Further the Board finds
that issuing general obligation bonds relating to the Improvement District is the most attainable
and beneficial option for obtaining financing for the Improvement Projects, and as such, as
required by Education Code section 15301(c), it finds that the overall cost of issuing general
obligation bonds would be less than the overall cost of other school facilities financing options
available to the District, if any, including, but not limited to, forming a community facilities district
and issuing bonds pursuant to the Mello-Roos Act.

          Section 10. Effective Date. This Resolution shall take effect immediately upon adoption
hereof.


      PASSED AND ADOPTED as Los Rios Community College District Resolution
No. 2026-04 this eleventh day of March 2026, by the following called vote:


 AYES:                              NAYES:                             ABSENT:

   SUBJECT:                 LRCEA Collective Bargaining            ATTACHMENT: None

   APPROVED FOR                                                    ACTION                          X

BACKGROUND:
The Los Rios Classified Employees Association (LRCEA) is the exclusively recognized representative of
classified professionals in the white-collar bargaining unit. The District and LRCEA entered into a
collectively bargained agreement in 2021, which was renewed through June 30, 2025. Following good
faith negotiations, the parties have reached tentative agreement on a successor contract for a three-
year period (January 2026 – December 2028). The tentative agreement was ratified by a majority vote
of LRCEA unit members.

Per Section 3547.5 of the Government Code, prior to entering into a written agreement with an exclusive
representative covering matters within the scope of representation, all public school employers are
required to disclose the major provisions of the agreement, including but not limited to, the costs
associated with the agreement. Although the State Chancellor’s Office has stated this statute does not
apply to community colleges, the District is required to disclose similar information to the State
Chancellor’s Office on certain financial reports. Given the significance of these agreements, public
disclosure, even if not specially required, is still appropriate and prudent.

STATUS:
The tentative agreement with LRCEA proposed for adoption features language clarifications, gender-
neutral pronouns, and administrative updates to reflect current practices and legislative changes.
Additionally, provisions from existing memoranda of understanding (MOUs) entered into during the
prior contract period have been incorporated. Major provisions of the agreement include:

   •   Article 2: Organizational Rights
           o Release LRCEA President full-time (40 hours per week) for conducting LRCEA business
               (Section 2.2.3);
           o Increase release time for LRCEA Treasurer and Secretary from one to two hours per week
               to conduct LRCEA business (Section 2.2.3);


                                                                                                  143
                                                                                                    HOME
   •   Article 4: Evaluation of the Job Performance
           o Update the length of most probationary periods from 12 months to six months, in
               accordance with state law (Section 4.8.1);
           o Adjust the timing of probationary and conditional evaluations (Sections 4.7.2 and 4.8.4);
           o Establish a subcommittee to update the Report of Job Performance evaluation form to
               include DEIA principles, in accordance with state law (Section 4.14);
   •   Article 6: Overtime
           o Update overtime provision to more accurately compensate employees for additional
               hours worked (Section 6.3.3);
   •   Article 7: Leaves with Pay
           o Increase maximum amount of vacation day accrual from 47.5 days to 60 days (Section
               7.16.8.3);
   •   Article 8: Leaves Without Pay
           o Increase maximum length of full-time educational leave from 12 months to 18 months
               (Section 8.7.1);
   •   Article 9: Compensation
           o Conduct a compensation market survey (Section 9.1.1);
           o Clarify shift differential language for purposes of compliance with CalPERS regulations
               (Section 9.6);
           o Clarify longevity language for purposes of compliance with CalPERS regulations (Section
               9.7);
           o Establish Bilingual Pay Pilot Program to compensate the use of required communication
               skills other than English with $250 per month (Section 9.14);
   •   Article 14: Transfers and Reassignments
           o Increase notice of administrative transfers to a different work location from 15 working
               days to 30 calendar days (Section 14.5.4.2);
           o Require newly-hired employees to complete probation to be eligible for a voluntary
               transfer or promotion (Section 14.6);
   •   Article 16: Professional Growth and Career Development
           o Memorialize existing practice for tuition reimbursement (Sections 16.1 and 16.3);
   •   Appendix A: Salary & Benefits
          o Reflect prior agreement to contribute to health savings accounts (HSAs) for eligible
             employees (Section A.2.3.1.2); and
          o Include CalPERS limit on reporting off salary schedule improvements (Section A.18).

RECOMMENDATION:
It is recommended that the Board of Trustees approve the disclosure information and adopt the
collective bargaining agreement with the Los Rios Classified Employees Association for the period of
January 1, 2026 – December 31, 2028.

             LOS RIOS COMMUNITY COLLEGE DISTRICT

SUBJECT:                  Contract Award: Management of              ATTACHMENT: None
                          District College Stores
                                                                     ENCLOSURE: None
                                                                     STRATEGIC PLAN GOAL(S): 5
AGENDA ITEM:              Action Item A                              TYPE OF BOARD CONSIDERATION:

                                                                     CONSENT/ROUTINE
RECOMMENDED BY:           Mario Rodriguez, Executive Vice
                          Chancellor, Finance and                    FIRST READING
                          Administration
APPROVED FOR                                                         ACTION                          X
CONSIDERATION:
                          Brian King, Chancellor                     INFORMATION

BACKGROUND:
The college store industry has shifted significantly in recent years. Increased competition from online
retailers and continued growth in Open Educational Resources (OER) and other low and no-cost course
materials have improved affordability for students but have also reduced traditional course materials
sales and increased financial volatility for the traditional outsourced college store business model.

To address these dynamics and modernize services, the District made the strategic decision to select a
qualified provider for management of college stores under a Hybrid Business Model. The Hybrid Service
Model maintains staffed on-ground campus stores at American River College and Sacramento City College,
while serving Folsom Lake College and Cosumnes River College through an Online Course Materials Store
(OCMS) and other designated access methods (including supplies vending machines), with course
materials distribution methods defined in coordination with each college. The RFP also emphasized
student affordability, improved course materials adoption tools and reporting, strong customer service,
technology/accessibility requirements, and data privacy/security expectations.

STATUS:
The RFP was publicly advertised and evaluated by a multi-stakeholder committee representing the
Colleges and District, including student, faculty, classified, and management perspectives. Based on the
committee’s evaluation and best-value determination, the committee recommends awarding the
contract to Barnes & Noble College Booksellers, LLC. The initial agreement term is July 1, 2026 through
June 30, 2031, with a one-year renewal option. Staff will coordinate implementation and transition
planning with the Colleges and stakeholders to ensure continuity of service.

Highlights aligned to the committee’s priorities include:
        • Highest overall evaluation results. Based on the committee’s scoring roll-up across all
             evaluation criteria and members, B&N ranked highest overall and had the highest cumulative
             points.
        • Responsiveness to RFP requirements. B&N accepted the District’s RFP requirements and
             confirmed key terms.
        • Hybrid model aligned to campus needs. Staffed, on-ground campus stores at American River
             College and Sacramento City College, with Folsom Lake College and Cosumnes River College
             served through the Online Course Materials Store (OCMS) and other designated access 145
             methods.
                                                                                                       HOME
       •   Student-centered operational commitments. Service standards, customer support
           expectations, and coordinated distribution methods to support timely student access to
           materials.
       •   Affordability, transparency, and compliance. Clear course materials pricing expectations,
           reporting and audit provisions, and requirements related to accessibility and data
           privacy/security.

RECOMMENDATION:
It is recommended that the Board of Trustees award the contract for management of District College
Stores to Barnes & Noble College Booksellers, LLC and authorize the Chancellor (or designee) to
negotiate and execute the final contract, effective July 1, 2026.

   SUBJECT:                  Folsom Lake College Artificial          ATTACHMENT: None
                             Intelligence (AI) Department
                                                                     ENCLOSURE: None
                                                                     STRATEGIC PLAN GOAL(S): 3
   AGENDA ITEM:              Information Item A                      TYPE OF BOARD CONSIDERATION:

                                                                     CONSENT/ROUTINE

                             Folsom Lake College President           FIRST READING

   APPROVED FOR                                                      ACTION
   CONSIDERATION:
                             Brian King, Chancellor                  INFORMATION                     X


BACKGROUND:
The AI Department at Folsom Lake College, established in 2024, is the second stand-alone AI Department
in the State of California. As it grows to include five certificates and an AS degree, the faculty are
providing leadership and support across the educational spectrum, while engaging with private industry
and local government. Collaborating with our local and regional communities, we are developing
seamless pathways for students to come to Folsom Lake College.

Central goals of the AI Department are to expand equitable access to high value AI education, diversifying
the field and supporting civic engagement in AI. This work includes helping to embed ethical, responsible,
and human-centered AI practices in all programs, collaborating across our campus and the Los Rios
Community College District. Recognized as leaders in this field, faculty in the AI Department are helping
to develop standards across the California Community College system and support K12 partners in
curriculum development.

STATUS:
Folsom Lake College will present an overview of the Artificial Intelligence (AI) Program.

RECOMMENDATION:
This item is presented for the Board of Trustees’ information and discussion.
